text:
I modified this slightly.  I  eliminated the ham since I was making a full ham to go with these.  I also eliminated the onion.  I used the cream of mushroom soup & one full soup can of milk instead of water.  Along with the chedder cheese I added about 3/4 C of mozz. cheese & monteray jack that I had in the fridge wanting to use up.  I also added about 3 cloves of crused garlic.  Everyone loved them!  I just threw everything in the crock pot very early in the day & kept it on low for  about 5 hours then went to high for the last hour.  Will be making again & again.

text:
This is very similiar to my recipe for slow cooker scalloped potatoes. My recipe is to butter the crockpot and layer half the potatoes, onions, seasonings, ham, and velveeta cheese. Repeat with second layer. Top with cream of chicken soup (or any other cream soup).  Sprinkle with papricka.   I cut the medium size potatoes in half before slicing thin.  Doing this reduces my cooking time to just less then 3 hours on high. Another tip is to soak the raw potatoes in 1 cup of water mixed with 1 teaspoon of cream of tartar to prevent the potatoes from browning, drain water before layering. This is a wonderfully delicious and easy dish.

text:
I followed the advice of the others and layered the ingredients. I also doubled the ham and cheese and used milk instead of water.  Instead of chopped ham, I used two whole bone in ham slices (each one being a separate layer). The bone gives it more flavor.  I added a few cloves of chopped garlic to the chopped onion. I had two layers of potatoes, onion/garlic, ham slice and cheese (cheese being on top).  Then I poured the soup mixture over the top. I used the amount of salt, pepper and garlic powder called for.  Cooked on high for four hours and then turned to low until dinner time, about two hours.  IT WAS DELICIOUS!!!! My husband is not a big potato fan and he LOVED this dish as did my college age son. It was a bit watery but I turned it on high for about 20 minutes with the lid off prior to serving and that took care of it plus filled the house with a wonderful aroma! Reheated the leftovers in the crock pot the next day and it was even better! I will definitely make this again and won't change a thing from the above. I don't think it could possibly be improved upon!

This was very good! I've made it twice now, both times with rave reviews. I followed the advice of another reviewer and cooked it in the oven at 325 for 1-1/2 hours. I used milk instead of water. I cooked it covered with foil until the last 15 minutes, sprinkled the top with shredded cheese, then seasoned bread crumbs over the cheese. It created a flavorful crunchy, cheesey topping. Yummy! I have also microwaved the sliced potatoes to shorten the cooking time. I am looking forward to the day when I have time to try it in the crockpot.

text:
This is delicious with or without cheese. But when I do add cheese, I use 2 cups and I always use milk, not water with this recipe. One other thing - leave out the salt. There is already plenty of sodium in the soup, the cheese and most certainly the ham. It's just not necessary to add more from the shaker. I have made this both in the slow cooker and in the oven (2 quart casserole dish, bake at 350 degrees covered for 1 hour, then uncovered for an additional 1/2 hour). Both ways come out yummy! Whichever method you use, layer the ingredients and be sure to slice your potatoes very thin. Oh, and I also don't peal the potatoes before slicing. I just clean them well and slice away. There is fiber and lots of nutrients in the skin. Enjoy!!

text:
Double the amount of potatoes and ham. Use TWO cans of Cream Of Mushroom. Also add a package of Country Style gravy to the mushroom soup and water.   I always throw in Garlic Powder, Basil & Penzey's Black & Red (cayenne / black pepper). I never measure out the cheese - I just throw on Sharp Cheddar until I think it's enough (only for the last half hour of cooking).  Perfectly saucy (thickens up as it cools) and utterly delish.   3.5 - 4 hours on HIGH in the Crock pot. Before cooking, toss the potatoes in cup of water with a 1/2 tsp cream of tartar - to keep 'em from getting dark while cooking  *UPDATE* Today, I needed to use up 3/4 cup of Heavy Cream, and then added just short of 1 1/2 cups of water (in place of the 2 cups water).  This small change really upped the WOW factor!

country:
None
text:
I made this recipe but made the mistake of not thinly slicing the potatoes.  If anyone has ended up with a watery mixture because of having to cook it longer than the 4 hrs, this might be the problem.  If this happens to you, this is how to fix it, and as a result, you will still have an amazing thick cheesy comfort meal!  
You will need 1 cup of milk, 2 TBSP flour and 1-2 cups of shredded chedder cheese (depending on how cheesy you like it.

In a pan on low heat, whisk constantly milk and flour until thick and hot but not scolded or boiling (about 30 secs-1 min). Take off heat, and add anywhere between 1-2 cups of cheese.  It must be EXTREMELY thick (thicker than pancake batter) because it must stand up to the watered down mixture in the crock.  I added additional onion & garlic powders, and salt. Whisk for a minute until shredded cheese is melted.  Mix into ham and potatoes in crockpot. I like it very thick, so I let it sit for a bit to let the mixture thicken more. It's even better if you refrigerate overnight and heat the next day.  The flavors are even better and so much thicker!!

text:
Very easy and tasty - my husband is a big fan of ham and scalloped potatoes so I just had to make this for him! I did tweak the recipe a bit. I more than doubled the amount of ham and used a whole vidalia onion layering it in the crock pot first along with light shredded cheddar cheese. I mixed 98% fat free cream of mushroom soup with an equal can of fat free half and half vs. water.  I used fresh minced garlic vs. powdered. I poured that over everything and let it go on high for 4 hours. Since it didn't seem creamy enough I added 4 oz. light cream cheese and another 1/2 cup of shredded cheese. I cooked it for another two hours and it thickend up and was a lot creamier. My husband asked for seconds so it's a definite winner!

I loved this idea.  First time to try scalloped potatoes in a slow cooker and with a few changes it turned out to be one of the family's favorites.  I left out the cheese and garlic powder and put a full ham slice bone in on top of the potatoes as they cooked.  And added kernel corn on each layer. The flavour of the ham went through the potatoes.  I also put another spin on it by laying pork chops on top.  Both versions were absolutely stupendous.

I made this without ham, since I was bringing it to a friend's dinner where the main dish was ham. I took some of the other suggestions - used milk instead of water, doubled the cheese, layered the ingredients. Also cooked for about 6 hours on low before unplugging and bringing it to dinner, where it sat for another 1.5 hours on high. I was worried that the potatoes were still underdone, but they were just about right.... could have been a little bit more cooked, for my taste, but everyone else said they were great. And I sliced the potatoes really thin. I think next time I would add even more cheese, and fresh garlic. Thanks for the recipe - slow cooker recipes are the best for potlucks and dinners where everyone is pitching in.

text:
This recipe is the ultimate in family-friendly comfort food. I made this as written, and absolutely loved the results! I saw no need to add extra water...there was plenty of the soup mixture to cover all of the other ingredients. This came out perfectly creamy and yummy! The only change I made was to double the recipe and layer it in my slow cooker instead of mixing it all together...I put in a layer of potatoes, then a layer of the cheese/onion/ham mixture, and than a layer of the soup mix. I repeated this process and made about 4 layers altogether. It was super easy to make, and my family absolutely loved it! Thanks for sharing...this one is definitely going to be a regular in my meal rotation!

text:
My family LOVED this recipe! I followed some of the other suggestions and used the Cream of Mushroom soup with garlic and still added the 1/2 tsp. garlic powder. We also double the amount of ham (cut into 1/4" cubes) and used 1-1/2 cups cheese. I cooked it on high for 5 hours. When putting it into the crockpot, it definitely helps to layer the potatoes, cheese/onion/ham mixture, and the soup as you do not want to stir this until the very end to prevent breaking up the potato slices.

I will definitely make this recipe again!!

But as in other reviews i made some modifications.  I used 1 can milk and 1 of half and half. I also lightly sauted 2 finely minced cloves garlic  added cream of mushroom soup the cream,milk and Swanson concentrated liquid chicken broth  (i don't have a problem w too much salt)  I don't add extra salt anywhere in recipe. Oh so good and you'll learn  to love your spinach. And you have a complete meal. I gave recipe 5stars because basic recipe has great potential.

text:
We love this, but we make it just a little differently. First, we have a 6 QT crockpot so this puts our potatoes in a thinner layer on the bottom of the dish. This means the potatoes cook a little faster. Also, I don't slice potatoes anymore in any scalloped potato recipe. instead I cube it up fairly small, like 1/2 inch to 1/4 inch pieces. I use cream of celery for allergy reasons but also it has good flavor. I also use fresh garlic, one extra large clove. I didn't have ham but I did have a big bag of bacon bits from Costco, and figured it would actually taste better that way. I added a 1/4 cup milk on top of the water and probably had an extra lb of potato in there too but the flavor was really spectacular. We occasionally cook a ring of (pre-cooked) sausage on top of these, poke it so the juices run and away we go!

I have been making this recipe since Campbell's Soup put out their original cookbook back in the 60's. I omit the cheese and I place a layer of potatoes, then onions, then ham and keep repeating layers. Then cover with soup mixture. As I do not have a slow cooker, I put it in A 2 QUART CASSEROLE DISH, COVER AND BAKE AT 375 FOR 1 HOUR.I THEN REMOVE COVER FOR THE REMAINING 1/2 HOUR. Any leftovers are really good fried the next day.

After reading other reviews, I changed this slightly.  I used 1 1/2 lbs of small russett potatoes, a 16oz pkg of diced ham and 2 cups of shredded cheddar. I would say this recipe deserves 4 stars only after changes have been made. I added extra ham, cheese, used heavy cream instead of water and added a few other spices(cayenne, garlic powder). I cooked for 5 hours on high in my crock pot and the potatoes were not even close to being done and they were watery.  I put them in a casserole dish minus the liquid and put some extra cheese on the top and finished them in the oven. text:
Scalloped potatoes is a layered dish. So you do a layer of potatoes, a layer of cheese/meat/onion, another layer of potatoes, another layer of meat etc. Last layer should be potatoes.

If you like cheese on top, put that on the last 30 minutes or so. That way it melts, but doesn't dissolve into the sauce.

"put in the crock pot"  Which? The 1.5 quart, the 5 quart or the 10 quart? The 5 quart was perfect, and it makes 10 servings at least.

I do not use canned soup. Instead, I made a sauce of 4 cups of cashew milk, 2T mushroom powder, .5t salt, and garlic and onion powder to taste.  This is considerably more liquid that the recipe called for, but made a really rich creamy sauce.

I used milk instead of water, added another cup of cheese, and added some paprika and lots of garlic salt. I wasn't able to make this in a crock pot since I'm at work for too long. I cooked it at 350 for two hours and it still wasn't done, so I turned it up to 375 and cooked it for another hour. Moral of the story:  it takes forever to cook potatoes in the oven so do it on the weekend, or use the crock pot if you can.

Loved this recipe. Much lighter than traditional scalloped potatoes. I opted to bake this at 350 in the oven. Baked it for an hour in an 13x9 dish using 7-8 medium yellow/gold potatoes and a maple ham steak, diced. Stirred after an hour and cooked it for another 15 minutes to be sure potatoes were done. It didn't seem to have enough sauce so that is why I stirred it. In the end it proved to be a very nice and light, roasted-potatoes consistency, with a light sauce. Great flavor!

text:
This was very good for an easy recipe but it would have been better with added spices (maybe minced garlic and paprika?)I started it off on high and my potatoes started to burn at the sides of the crockpot. I did use cooking spray before adding the ingredients but it helped only on the bottom. I used water as stated but later when everything started getting too thick and dry, I added a little milk. Also, I didn't add the ham and cheese at the start. I waited until about an hour before serving to add the ham, then a little later, slices of sharp cheddar cheese (I was in too much of a hurry to grate it). I read so many reviews where the cheese got lost in the mix so though this way would be better. I let it melt a bit, then stirred gently. This cheese was very yummy in it. I think it helped that I used sharp cheese since I didn't even put the 1 cup the recipe called for.

It's in the slowcooker as we speak. I read all the reviews and used many of the suggestions. My BIG tip is to use a apple peeler/corer! Makes quick work with peeling and slicking. I used 8 medium whites. The potato cores were sliced and frozen for future breakfast potato!

two cloves of garlic rather than powder
cream rather than water
1 cup of onion
double the ham (had spare bone in ham leftover in the freezer)
4 shitake mushrooms
added edam cheese to the cheddar (had some in the fridge)

Used milk instead of water & added 1 T butter because I like my scalloped pots with butter in them for flavor. The only problem I had was my crockpot must be very hot on 'high' (it's only a yr old) because I had to turn it to 'low'. It had (really) stuck to the pot only part-way through. Hint: If you want to add flavor to something, add butter &/or cheese (adding cheese can also help 'cover up' any 'errors' or enhance a dish).  TASTED GREAATTT! I've never rated anything on here before but if it's based on a 5-star rating. That's what "I" give it for taste and ease. Just check your crockpot for best setting.

text:
We loved this recipe!  I've had a hard time finding the perfect scalloped potato recipe and was surprised that this is it.  I doubled the ham and cheese (used swiss), used some dehydrated onion flakes instead of fresh onion and didn't have any cream soups so made my own.  I brought 1 1/2 cups milk, 1 cup water, a chicken bouillon cube, salt, pepper, parsley and the garlic powder to a boil and stirred in 3 tablespoons flour mixed into half a cup of milk.  Let it boil for a couple of minutes and then poured it over the layered ham, potatoes and cheese.  Mine needed 3 hours to cook.  Next time I'll use 2 cups of the "soup" instead of 3.  Thanks for the great idea!

text:
My family and I found this to be a yummy recipe with a few changes made.  I only used about 1/4 cup milk for the liquid and I added about a cup of cottage cheese as well as 4 slices of american cheese.  I also used 2 cups reduced fat cabot cheddar cheese and reduced fat mushroom soup.  I stirred about once an hour and cooked about 5 hours on high.  The result was creamy, comforting and tasty!

text:
I usually use my own recipe so I decided to use this one instead, for a change.  Unfortunately, I had to modify it a bit.  I used one whole onion by mistake but it didn't affect anything.  I used a slow cooker liner to prevent having to clean the crockpot.  That's a must!

Then I added an 8 oz. bag of cubed ham, used a 26 oz. can of mushroom soup, diluted it with a couple dashes of milk so it wouldn't come out soupy and used 2 cups of cheddar cheese.  It was done in 4 hours as promised but it was still a bit soupy so I left the lid off for about 30 minutes & it firmed up nice.

I couldn't taste the cheese, so next time I will omit it and it was a bit salty so I will omit that also.  This is a very good recipe & I'll use it again.

city:

region:
None
country:
None
text:
ive noticed some people had problems with this recipe.  Couple of tips... 1, know your slow cooker. Ive yet to see two different  slow cookers cook the same meal in the same amount of time.
2.  I don't much cook with salt .. you can always add salt at the table.  Ham comes a few ways, fresh, salt cured or smoked.  Go for the lower salt option, i prefer smoke cured.  and remember, you can always soak your ham the night before in your fridge in cold water to draw salt out. I don't believe Fresh would work for this recipe 3. Using Soup. canned soup can be salty and the lo salt versions, imho, are nasty. if salt doesn't bother you, then use the canned, but use at least a premium brand, bargain canned soup.. well, there's a reason its a bargain. I prefer the broccoli cheddar soup for this. 4. if you don't  want Soup -try the alternative, make a roux, with real butter, good flour and  real cream or half and half, and do not cook on high.  always cook on low when using real cream or half and half, too high a temp causes it to separate and/or sour. 5. layer your potatoes, onions etc.  6. you can never have too much cheese in scalloped potatoes. Don't be afraid to add more.
Lastly, every single recipe that i've ever used from this site, I've altered to my family's taste. Think about what you and your family like and adjust accordingly :) This is a great easy recipe, and just like all recipes, think it through :)

text:
I've made this for the past two Thanksgivings and it was a hit. I did make a few changes. I doubled the cheese and didn't bother peeling the potatoes. I added a lot more garlic and black pepper. I used a little extra water in the soup because it was a little too thick and didn't mix well with all the potatoes. I added just a touch of salt and left out the ham because we were going to have plenty of protein with the turkey and because we felt it would add too much salt to the dish. The leftovers are usually among the first to disappear after Thanksgiving. I will continue to make this every Thanksgiving going forward, and maybe a few times in between.
